# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir`

# Grafana Plugin Backend Query to Data Frame Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a Grafana datasource plugin query flows from the HTTP API handler to a data frame response. Find Go source files in grafana/grafana implementing: the query API handler, the plugin client call, the backend query execution, and the data frame serialization.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

59-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the analysis and created the `answer.json` file with comprehensive findings about the Grafana datasource plugin query chain.

## Summary

I've traced the complete flow of how a Grafana datasource plugin query travels from the HTTP API handler to a data frame response. Here's what I found:

### Key Components in the Query Chain:

1. **HTTP Query Endpoint** (`pkg/api/ds_query.go:QueryMetricsV2`)
   - Receives POST requests to `/api/ds/query`
   - Delegates to the query service

2. **Query Service Orchestration** (`pkg/services/query/query.go:ServiceImpl`)
   - Core routing logic for single/multi-datasource queries
   - Routes single datasource queries through `handleQuerySingleDatasource`

3. **Plugin Client** (`pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/`)
   - `ClientV2`: Handles protobuf conversion and gRPC communication
   - `protoClient`: Provides the low-level gRPC interface

4. **Plugin API Handler** (`pkg/aggregator/apiserver/plugin/query.go:QueryDataHandler`)
   - HTTP handler that executes the actual plugin query
   - Returns wrapped QueryDataResponse

5. **Data Frame Serialization**
   - Response serialization through `response.JSONStreaming()`
   - Uses Apache Arrow encoding for efficient data transfer

The complete flow is: **HTTP POST /api/ds/query → QueryMetricsV2 → queryData → handleQuerySingleDatasource → pluginClient.QueryData (gRPC) → Plugin Backend → QueryDataResponse with Frames → toJsonStreamingResponse → JSON HTTP Response**

The answer file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json` with all relevant files, symbols, and a detailed explanation of the query chain.

Plugin Client Abstraction (pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/)\\nThe plugin client layer bridges Grafana core with backend plugins:\\n\\n**ClientV2** (pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/client_v2.go):\\n- The `QueryData()` method (line 162) receives `backend.QueryDataRequest`\\n- Converts request to protobuf: `backend.ToProto().QueryDataRequest(req)`\\n- Calls `c.DataClient.QueryData(ctx, protoReq)` through gRPC\\n- Receives protobuf response and converts back: `backend.FromProto().QueryDataResponse(protoResp)`\\n\\n**ProtoClient** (pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/client_proto.go):\\n- The `QueryData()` method (line 113) provides the gRPC client interface\\n- Gets the `ClientV2` instance and delegates to `c.DataClient.QueryData(ctx, in, opts...)`\\n- This makes the actual gRPC call to the plugin process\\n\\n#### 5. Plugin API Handler (pkg/aggregator/apiserver/plugin/query.go:QueryDataHandler)\\nThis is the HTTP handler that the aggregator/plugin server implements:\\n- Receives `QueryDataRequest` as JSON\\n- Extracts datasource UID from URL path\\n- Gets plugin context through `h.pluginContextProvider.GetPluginContext()`\\n- Calls `h.client.QueryData()` to execute the actual plugin\\n- Wraps response in `aggregationv0alpha1.QueryDataResponse`\\n- Returns serialized response through HTTP\\n\\n#### 6.
